It is a perfect way to implement common patterns: auth, logging, and monitoring.\n\n## Error Handling Patterns\n\nOn the server side, you can write a logging interceptor so that it looks for any unhandled errors and logs it with any metadata associated with the request, which will be useful to identify and correlate the failure to the request, and you can also perform a translation of the error message to a more user friendly error.\n\nInterceptor intercepts API requests and records information like duration, error code and etc, and will intercept API request and record request metadata into metrics.\n\n## Monitoring with Prometheus and Grafana\n\nFor monitoring gRPC services with Grafana and Prometheus, to use Interceptors in chains, refer to go-grpc-middleware. Handles specific status codes (404, 500) with default messages, settable via the message parameter.\n\n**Err()** - Processes `errutil.Error` types specifically, extracting HTTP status from the error's reason and returning the public-facing error data. Returns 500 Internal Server Error if the error isn't an `errutil.Error`.\n\n**ErrOrFallback()** - Provides fallback behavior by checking if an error is an `errutil.Error` first. If not, it checks for `context.Canceled` and returns a canceled request error, otherwise uses the provided status and message as defaults.\n\n## Standard Response Functions\n\n**Success()** - Generates a 200 OK response containing `{\"message\": \"<provided message>\"}`.\n\n**Empty()** - Returns a response with no body content at the specified status code.\n\n**Respond()** - Base response builder that marshals various body types ([]byte, string, nil, or JSON-serializable objects) into responses.\n\n## Specialized Response Functions\n\n**JSON()** / **JSONStreaming()** - Create JSON responses with appropriate content-type headers; streaming variant buffers output for large payloads.\n\n**YAML()** / **YAMLDownload()** - Generate YAML responses using text/yaml or application/yaml with optional download headers.\n\n**JSONDownload()** - JSON response with attachment disposition for file downloads.\n\n**Redirect()** - Produces HTTP 302 redirect responses."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_0151S4iJ9RUZpAn1cJAtdFTM","session_id":"1734e9e5-d5ff-490f-81f7-69630af6b6c4","uuid":"abcf9ef3-79ab-4d34-8b06-d20c7f5bdf46"}

PermissionDenied can follow a valid authentication but failed authorization step.\n\n## Key Distinction\n\nAn important distinction: PermissionDenied must not be used if the caller cannot be identified (use Unauthenticated instead for those errors). Services\\n\\n### Kubernetes/Kubernetes\\n\\nKubernetes uses a hierarchical error architecture that bridges gRPC status codes to HTTP responses through its API machinery layer.\\n\\n**Error Creation**: The primary error creation functions are in `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors/errors.go`. These functions (NewNotFound, NewConflict, NewInternalError, etc.) create StatusError instances with hardcoded HTTP status codes (404, 409, 500, etc.). These are Kubernetes domain-specific errors, not direct gRPC status codes.\\n\\n**gRPC Error Detection**: In `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/rest.go`, the REST handler explicitly imports gRPC codes and status packages and detects gRPC errors through interface checking. The `isTooLargeError()` function (line 457) checks for both etcd errors (codes.InvalidArgument with \\\"request is too large\\\" message) and gRPC errors (codes.ResourceExhausted). This detection happens at the request scope level.\\n\\n**Error Translation Chain**: The translation path flows through three main stages:\\n1. Error creation or detection (NewNotFound, isTooLargeError)\\n2. Conversion to metav1.Status via `ErrorToAPIStatus()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/responsewriters/status.go`, which maps gRPC status codes to HTTP codes (lines 34-83)\\n3. HTTP response rendering via `ErrorNegotiated()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/responsewriters/writers.go`\\n\\n**CRI Integration**: The Kubelet's Container Runtime Interface has dedicated error handling in `staging/src/k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/cri/streaming/errors.go`, where `WriteError()` directly translates gRPC codes (codes.NotFound → 404, codes.ResourceExhausted → 429) to HTTP responses for streaming endpoints.\\n\\n**gRPC Rate Limiting**: `pkg/kubelet/apis/grpc/ratelimit.go` creates gRPC status errors directly via `status.Error(codes.ResourceExhausted, ...)` for rate limiting scenarios, handled by the LimiterUnaryServerInterceptor.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\nGrafana implements error handling at multiple layers with explicit gRPC code usage in interceptors and protobuf-based error response structures.\\n\\n**gRPC Interceptor Level**: In `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go`, authentication errors are created using `status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, ...)` and `status.Error(codes.PermissionDenied, ...)` directly at the unary/stream interceptor level. These are created early in the request pipeline before any business logic executes.\\n\\n**Resource Server Error Layer**: The unified resource storage layer (`pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go`) provides error constructors like `NewBadRequestError()` and `NewNotFoundError()` that create custom error types. These include HTTP status codes directly in the error definition. The `AsErrorResult()` function converts errors to protobuf ErrorResult messages with explicit HTTP status codes embedded.\\n\\n**Resource Server Operations**: Files like `pkg/storage/unified/resource/server.go` implement CRUD operations (Create, Read, Update, Delete) that return errors with HTTP status codes. These errors bubble up to the HTTP layer.\\n\\n**HTTP Response Translation**: In `pkg/api/response/response.go`, the `Err()` function extracts HTTP status from errutil.Error types and renders them as HTTP responses. The `ErrOrFallback()` function handles context.Canceled errors and falls back to default status codes when needed.\\n\\n**Dashboard Error Mapping**: The `pkg/api/apierrors/dashboard.go` file contains `ToDashboardErrorResponse()` function that comprehensively maps various error types (including Kubernetes API errors and plugin errors) to HTTP responses using type assertions and error comparisons.\\n\\n**Proto Definition**: `pkg/storage/unified/proto/resource.proto` defines ErrorResult message with fields for HTTP status code suggestion, making the gRPC-to-HTTP mapping explicit in the protocol definition.\\n\\n### etcd-io/etcd\\n\\netcd uses a clear two-layer error system: domain errors that map to gRPC status errors via a centralized conversion function, which can then be translated to HTTP.\\n\\n**Error Definition Layer**: `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` is the primary error definition file containing 60+ gRPC status error constants (ErrGRPCEmptyKey with codes.InvalidArgument, ErrGRPCKeyNotFound with codes.NotFound, ErrGRPCNoLeader with codes.Unavailable, ErrGRPCInvalidAuthToken with codes.PermissionDenied, etc.). The `Error()` function converts gRPC errors to EtcdError structs, and `ErrorDesc()` extracts messages.\\n\\n**Domain Error Layer**: `server/etcdserver/errors/errors.go` defines domain-specific errors (ErrNoLeader, ErrStopped, ErrTimeout, ErrCanceled) that are internal to the server implementation and don't directly use gRPC codes.\\n\\n**Centralized Conversion**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go` contains the critical `togRPCError()` function that maps all internal errors to gRPC status errors via the `toGRPCErrorMap`. This is the single point where domain errors become gRPC errors. The function distinguishes between client context errors (which pass through) and server errors (which get mapped).\\n\\n**RPC Handler Usage**: Multiple RPC handler files use togRPCError for conversion:\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go`: Key-value operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/auth.go`: Authentication operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/lease.go`: Lease operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/member.go`: Cluster member operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/watch.go`: Watch stream operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/quota.go`: Storage quota enforcement\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/maintenance.go`: Maintenance operations\\n\\n**HTTP Translation**: `server/etcdserver/api/etcdhttp/utils.go` contains `writeError()` function that translates errors to HTTP responses. It handles both v2error.Error types and generic errors, mapping them to appropriate HTTP status codes.\\n\\n**HTTP Peer Endpoints**: `server/etcdserver/api/etcdhttp/peer.go` uses `allowMethod()` for HTTP verb validation (returns 405) and maps specific error types to HTTP codes using error.Is() checks (e.g., ErrIDNotFound → 404, ErrMemberNotLearner → 412).\\n\\n**gRPC Server Configuration**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/grpc.go` sets up the gRPC server with appropriate message size limits and interceptors, establishing the infrastructure where gRPC status codes are created and propagated.\\n\\n**gRPC Interceptors**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/interceptor.go` validates capabilities and returns errors like rpctypes.ErrGRPCNotCapable early in the request chain, ensuring errors are caught before expensive operations.\\n\\n### Comparative Analysis\\n\\n**Kubernetes** creates Kubernetes-specific error types (not direct gRPC codes) that include HTTP status codes, detecting gRPC errors from external services and converting them through ErrorToAPIStatus().\\n\\n**Grafana** uses explicit gRPC status codes at the interceptor level combined with protobuf-based error messages that embed HTTP status codes, making the translation point explicit in the proto definition.\\n\\n**etcd** maintains a clean separation: domain errors → centralized togRPCError() conversion → HTTP translation via writeError(). This design makes error mapping explicit and auditable in a single location (toGRPCErrorMap).\\n\\nAll three projects handle the fundamental challenge of bridging gRPC's status code system with HTTP status codes, but they do so at different architectural layers: Kubernetes at the API server layer, Grafana through protobuf-embedded status codes, and etcd through explicit conversion mapping.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6283,"cache_read_input_tokens":24819,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6283},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1734e9e5-d5ff-490f-81f7-69630af6b6c4","uuid":"f4fe7a35-6112-4e17-a6c4-e1263f0bb673"}
